Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Parsing the Front Matter of an Islamic Scholarly Work
Book cover and author biography page

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and interpret the key elements of a scholarly book's front matter, including title, publisher, author credentials, and thematic clues.

Core Idea
The front page of a scholarly work is a contract of authority and purpose.

Before diving into the content of any scholarly work, the front matter provides essential context: who wrote it, who published it, and what the author wants you to know upfront. In this lesson, we examine the opening page of Dr. Ahmad al-Daghashy's 'Nazariyya Quran' to see how these elements frame the entire work.

Guided Path
1
Identify the title and its significance
Look at the main title: 'نظرية المعرفة في القرآن الكريم وتضميناتها التربوية' (Theory of Knowledge in the Noble Quran and its Educational Implications). The partial verse 'Not equal are those who know and those who do not know' reinforces the epistemological theme.
The title tells you this book is about epistemology (nazariyyat al-ma'rifa) grounded in the Quran and applied to education.
2
Identify the publisher and its role
The publisher is listed as 'المعهد العالمي للفكر الاسلامي' (IIIT) and 'دار الفكر' in Damascus. IIIT is a major institution for Islamic thought, signaling the work's academic and reformist orientation.
Knowing the publisher helps assess the scholarly community and editorial standards.
3
Extract the author's academic credentials
The author holds two PhDs: one in Philosophy of Islamic Education from Yarmouk University, another in Foundations of Islamic Education from University of Khartoum. He is a faculty member at Sana'a University. These credentials establish his authority.
List the universities and degrees to gauge the author's expertise in Islamic education and epistemology.
4
Note the author's other works
The author's list of publications includes books on fitrah, theory of knowledge, Gulf crisis, critical studies, and women's jurisprudence. This indicates his broader thematic interests and scholarly output.
This helps situate the current work within the author's overall project.

الأبحاث
Those who know and those who do not know are not equal. The International Institute of Islamic Thought. Dar al-Fikr for Printing and Distribution, Damascus - Syria. Theory of Knowledge in the Noble Quran and its Educational Implications. Dr. Ahmad Muhammad Husayn al-Daghashy. Ahmad Muhammad Husayn al-Daghashy - born in Sana'a governorate 1966 - PhD in Philosophy of Islamic Education from Yarmouk University - and another in Foundations of Islamic Education from the University of Khartoum - faculty member at Sana'a University (College of Education). He has: The Fitrah Foundation in Islamic Education, Theory of Knowledge in the Quran and its Educational Implications, Positions of Islamists on the Gulf Crisis, Critical Reformist Studies, Four Preliminary Introductions in Issues of Women's Jurisprudence, and a number of research papers.
Source pages p. 1

Commentary
This passage is the front matter of the book 'Nazariyya Quran'. It displays the book title 'Theory of Knowledge in the Noble Quran and its Educational Implications' and the author's name. The opening line is a partial Quranic verse (Az-Zumar:9) 'Not equal are those who know and those who do not know,' which sets the epistemological theme. The publisher is the International Institute of Islamic Thought (IIIT) and Dar al-Fikr in Damascus. The author, Dr. Ahmad Muhammad Husayn al-Daghashy, was born in 1966 in Sana'a. He holds two doctorates: one in Philosophy of Islamic Education from Yarmouk University and another in Foundations of Islamic Education from the University of Khartoum. He is a faculty member at Sana'a University's College of Education. His other works include books on fitrah in Islamic education, theory of knowledge, Islamist perspectives on the Gulf crisis, critical reformist studies, and women's jurisprudence. This page serves as an introduction to the author's credentials and the scope of the work.

Key Terms

دار الفكر

Key Takeaway
The front matter of an Islamic scholarly work provides essential context about the author's credentials, the institutional backing, and the thematic focus, which are critical for evaluating the work's authority and relevance.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Find the front matter of another Islamic scholarly book (e.g., 'Al-Risala' by al-Shafi'i or 'Al-Muwatta' by Malik) and identify: the full title, publisher, author's credentials, and any thematic clues from the opening lines.
?
Write one paragraph explaining how the front matter of that work establishes the author's authority and the book's scope.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Parsing Author Biography and Institutional Context
Front matter presenting the author's credentials and the publisher's mission.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract and verify key biographical and institutional details from an Islamic book's front matter and evaluate their relevance to the work's authority.

Core Idea
A book's authority hinges on the author's credentials and the publisher's intellectual mission.

When you pick up a book on Islamic thought, the front matter often contains crucial clues about the author's academic preparation and the publisher's ideological orientation. In this passage, we meet Dr. Ahmad al-Dughshi and the International Institute of Islamic Thought. Learning to parse this information helps you critically assess the sources you use in your research and study.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's full name
Locate the author's name and list his academic degrees (PhDs) and university affiliations.
Dr. al-Dughshi has two PhDs: one in Islamic Education Philosophy and another in Foundations of Islamic Education.
2
List the author's publications
Scan the list of works he has authored. Notice the variety: from foundational works on Islamic education to contemporary issues.
One of his works is the very book you are studying: 'Nazariyyat al-Ma'rifa fi al-Qur'an'.
3
Examine the publisher's mission
Read Dar al-Fikr's mission and methodology. What values does it emphasize? (e.g., heritage, renewal, scientific revision)
Dar al-Fikr was established in 1957 and focuses on 'breaking monopolies of knowledge'.
4
Identify the sponsoring institution
The International Institute of Islamic Thought (IIIT) is also mentioned. What is its goal? How does it relate to the book?
IIIT aims at Islamizing knowledge and reforming contemporary Islamic thought.

Dar al-Fikr for Printing, Distribution and Publishing
Established in 1957 CE (1376 AH). Its mission: - Providing society with thought that illuminates the path to a better future. - Breaking monopolies of knowledge, and establishing a culture of dialogue. - Fueling the flame of thought with continuous renewal. Building direct bridges with the reader to achieve cultural interaction. Respecting intellectual property rights and calling for their respect. Its methodology:
- It proceeds from heritage as roots upon which it bases, builds upon without stopping at it, and circles around it. It selects its publications by standards of creativity, science, need, and future, and rejects imitation and repetition and what has passed its time. It cares for adult culture, and aspires to qualify children to build a reading society. All its works are subject to scientific, educational, and linguistic revision according to a guide and its own methodology.
It prepares its plans and programs for publication, and announces them: monthly, quarterly, annually, and for longer periods.
It relies on an elite of thinkers in addition to its own editorial, research, and translation departments. Its services and activities
First voracious reader club of its kind in the Arab world) annually gives its awards for literary creativity and criticism, and honors its authors and readers.
- Pioneering in electronic publishing
-
The International Institute of Islamic Thought
An independent Islamic cultural intellectual foundation established and registered in the United States of America at the beginning of the fifteenth century AH (1401 AH / 1981 CE) to work on: Providing a comprehensive Islamic vision in rooting and clarifying the universal issues of Islam and linking particulars and branches to universals, purposes, and general Islamic goals. Restoring the intellectual, cultural, and civilizational identity of the Islamic nation through efforts to Islamize the humanities and social sciences.
Reforming contemporary Islamic thought methodologies to enable directing and guiding the human civilization march and linking it to Islamic values and goals.
The institute uses means including: Holding specialized scientific and intellectual conferences and seminars.
Supporting the efforts of scholars and researchers in universities and scientific research centers, and publishing distinguished scientific output. Directing scientific and academic studies to serve issues of thought and knowledge.
The institute has a number of offices in many capitals
The first renewed Arabic site for an Arab publisher on the Internet: Arabic and Islamic, and others, and it also has cooperation agreements

www.zamzamworld.com

Source pages p. 2

Commentary
This passage is front matter providing biographical information about the author Ahmad Muhammad Husayn al-Dughshi and details about the two publishing entities: Dar al-Fikr and The International Institute of Islamic Thought. It begins with the author's birth year and academic credentials, listing his PhDs in Islamic education from Yarmouk and Khartoum universities, his teaching position at Sana'a University, and his previous publications. Then it describes Dar al-Fikr, established in 1957, emphasizing its mission to spread thought and knowledge, its methodology rooted in Islamic heritage, and its commitment to quality and innovation. Finally, it introduces The International Institute of Islamic Thought (IIIT), founded in 1981 in the USA, focusing on Islamizing knowledge and reforming contemporary Islamic thought through conferences, support for scholars, and publishing. The inclusion of this front matter indicates the institutional and academic context of the book.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Characteristics of Quranic Epistemology
Author introduces Quranic knowledge as comprehensive and eternal, outlining the book's epistemological approach.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four characteristics of Quranic knowledge and explain how they guide the development of an Islamic educational epistemology.

Core Idea
Quranic knowledge is comprehensive, integrated, eternal, and absolute.

This passage sets the foundation for the entire book: it declares that Quranic knowledge possesses unique features that compel us to derive a complete epistemological theory for Islamic education. Understanding these features is essential before exploring how revelation shapes knowledge in Islamic sciences.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four characteristics
Locate in the Arabic text the four adjectives describing Quranic knowledge: al-shumul, al-takamul, al-khulud, al-itlaqiyya. Write them down.
These are the pillars of the author's epistemology.
2
Understand why these characteristics matter
Reflect: how does each characteristic affect the way we derive knowledge from the Quran? For example, 'eternity' means the knowledge is valid for all times.
The author argues these characteristics 'push the researcher' to engage with revelation.
3
Outline the book's methodological structure
Trace the sequence: introduction to epistemology → nature of Quranic knowledge → linguistic/educational implications → sources, methods, limits → conclusion.
This is a systematic research plan, not random.
4
Recognize the author's epistemological goal
The final aim is an 'integrated theory of educational knowledge.' Note how the characteristics drive this goal.
This theory is meant to serve Islamic education today.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتسم المعرفة القرآنية بالشمول والتكامل والخلود والإطلاقية، على نحو يدفع الباحث للعمل على استنطاق نصوص الوحي الإلهي لاستخراج نظرية معرفية في التربية الإسلامية تلبي حاجة هذه التربية وتسهم في بلورة نظريتها المعاصرة. بدأ الكتاب بمدخل إلى نظرية المعرفة، ثم عرج على طبيعتها في القرآن الكريم وتضميناتها اللغوية والتربوية ومصادرها وطرائقها وحدودها، بأسلوب البحث المنهجي القائم على التتبع والأدلة. ليتوصل في النهاية إلى نظرية متكاملة للمعرفة التربوية يجدر الوقوف عندها وتأملها.
Quranic knowledge is characterized by comprehensiveness, integration, eternity, and absoluteness, in a way that pushes the researcher to work on eliciting from the texts of divine revelation an epistemological theory in Islamic education that meets the need of this education and contributes to crystallizing its contemporary theory. The book began with an introduction to epistemology, then turned to its nature in the Holy Quran and its linguistic and educational implications, its sources, methods, and limits, using systematic research based on investigation and evidence. Ultimately arriving at an integrated theory of educational knowledge worthy of contemplation and reflection.
Source pages p. 3

Commentary
This passage serves as an introduction to the book's methodology and content. It opens by defining four key characteristics of Quranic knowledge: comprehensiveness (shumul), integration (takamul), eternity (khulud), and absoluteness (itlaqiyya). These qualities compel the researcher to derive from revelation an epistemological theory tailored to Islamic education. The author then outlines the book's structure: it begins with a general introduction to epistemology, followed by an exploration of the nature of knowledge in the Quran, its linguistic and educational implications, its sources, methods, and limits. The approach is systematic, relying on investigation and evidence. The goal is to produce an integrated theory of educational knowledge that merits careful study.

Key Terms
المعرفة القرآنية
نظرية معرفية

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
Quranic knowledge possesses four defining features that mandate deriving a comprehensive, integrated, eternal, and absolute epistemological theory for Islamic education.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
Four Characteristics of Quranic Knowledge
Author introduces the characteristics of Quranic knowledge.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the four characteristics of Quranic knowledge as stated in the passage and explain how each one logically grounds the need for a distinct Islamic educational theory.

Core Idea
Quranic knowledge is comprehensively defined by four attributes: comprehensiveness, integration, eternity, and absoluteness.

This opening passage sets the stage for a work dedicated to extracting an epistemological theory from the Quran. The author begins by asserting four essential characteristics of Quranic knowledge—characteristics that, if taken seriously, compel the researcher to derive educational principles directly from revelation. In this lesson, you will learn to identify these characteristics and understand why they are presented as foundational for Islamic education.

Guided Path
1
Locate the four adjectives
In the Arabic text, find the four terms that describe Quranic knowledge: الشمول، التكامل، الخلود، الإطلاقية. These are the key attributes the author claims.
2
Define each characteristic concisely
Using context, write a one-sentence definition for each: al-shumul (comprehensiveness), al-takamul (integration), al-khulud (eternity), al-itlaqiyyah (absoluteness).
These are not merely descriptive; they are the logical basis for the author's project.
3
Derive the educational implication for each
For each characteristic, consider what it means for Islamic education. For example, comprehensiveness implies that education must cover all human domains, not just religious rituals.
4
Assess the author's epistemological move
Note that the author does not prove these characteristics from the Quran here; they are stated as given. The book promises to use systematic tracing and evidence to substantiate the theory. Ask yourself: are these characteristics self-evident from the Quran, or do they require demonstration?
This is a typical front-matter strategy: asserting a strong thesis to motivate the work.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
تتسم المعرفة القرآنية بالشمول والتكامل والخلود والإطلاقية، على نحو يدفع الباحث للعمل على استنطاق نصوص الوحي الإلهي لاستخراج نظرية معرفية في التربية الإسلامية تلبي حاجة هذه التربية وتسهم في بلورة نظريتها المعاصرة.
بدأ الكتاب بمدخل إلى نظرية المعرفة، ثم عرج على طبيعتها في القرآن الكريم وتضميناتها اللغوية والتربوية ومصادرها وطرائقها وحدودها، بأسلوب البحث المنهجي القائم على التتبع والأدلة.
ليتوصل في النهاية إلى نظرية متكاملة للمعرفة التربوية يجدر الوقوف عندها وتأملها.
بشه انه الخرز الحية
Quranic knowledge is characterized by comprehensiveness, integration, eternity, and absoluteness, in a way that pushes the researcher to work on eliciting the texts of divine revelation to extract an epistemological theory in Islamic education that meets the need of this education and contributes to crystallizing its contemporary theory. The book began with an introduction to epistemology, then touched upon its nature in the Holy Quran and its linguistic and educational implications, its sources, methods, and limits, using a systematic research method based on tracing and evidence. To finally arrive at an integrated theory of educational knowledge worthy of stopping at and contemplating. [Corrupt line: 'Bashah annahu al-khurz al-hayyah' unclear]
Source pages p. 4

Commentary
This passage is the opening statement of a work on Quranic epistemology. It is a front matter passage that sets out the author's motivation and approach. The author asserts that Quranic knowledge has four key attributes: comprehensiveness (al-shumul), integration (al-takamul), eternity (al-khulud), and absoluteness (al-itlaqiyyah). These qualities compel the researcher to interrogate the revealed texts in order to derive an epistemological theory for Islamic education that serves its needs and helps formulate its contemporary theory. The author then describes the structure of the book: it begins with an introduction to epistemology, then examines the nature of knowledge in the Quran, its linguistic and educational implications, its sources, methods, and limits. The research methodology is described as systematic, based on tracing (al-tatabbu') and evidence (al-adillah). The passage concludes by stating that the aim is to arrive at an integrated theory of educational knowledge worthy of reflection. The last line is corrupt but likely a basmalah. This is a typical preface outlining scope, method, and goals.

Key Terms

Reading an Islamic Book Title Page
Title page of a book on Quranic epistemology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to extract the title, author, publisher, and publication year from an Arabic Islamic book title page.

Core Idea
A book's title page is the gateway to its identity and scholarly context.

When you pick up an Islamic scholarly work, the title page provides essential information: the full title, author, publisher, and date. This lesson teaches you to interpret these details, which is the first step in any research. The passage you see is the title page of a book on Quranic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the title
Look for the longest phrase that names the book. It often begins with 'نظرية' or 'ال'. Here it is 'نظرية المعرفة في القرآن وتضميناتها التربوية'.
The title tells you the subject matter.
2
Find the author
After the title, you see the author's name: 'أحمد محمد حسين الدغشي'.
The author's name may appear before or after the title.
3
Locate the publisher
The publisher is 'دار الفكر' in Damascus, followed by the year 2001.
Publisher and place indicate the scholarly tradition.
4
Note the catalog number
The line 'ج ٢ ٤٧٢ ص' means volume 2, 472 pages. 'مكتبة الأسد' is the library cataloging it.
These details help locate the book in a library.

Parsing the Front Matter of an Islamic Epistemology Text
Publishing information and table of contents of a book on Quranic epistemology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the key components of a book's front matter and explain how they situate the work within Islamic thought.

Core Idea
Front matter reveals a book's scholarly lineage and epistemological framework before you read a single word.

Before engaging with the content of a book on Quranic epistemology, it is essential to understand its publication context, author, and structure. This lesson teaches you to extract meaningful information from front matter that can inform your approach to the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the title and subject
Locate the full title and any subject classification. Here, the title is 'نظرية المعرفة في القرآن' (Theory of Knowledge in the Quran) and the subject is 'القرآن وعلومه' (Quran and its sciences). This immediately tells you the book is about Quranic epistemology, not general logic.
2
Identify the author and his credentials
Find the author's name and any titles. The author is Dr. Ahmad Muhammad Husain al-Daghshi. The 'Dr.' indicates academic credentials, which may influence the book's methodological rigor.
3
Identify the publishing institutions
Note the publishers: the International Institute of Islamic Thought (IIIT) and Dar al-Fikr. IIIT is known for promoting Islamic epistemology and modern thought, which contextualises the book's approach.
4
Examine the table of contents for structure
The table of contents lists sections like 'مقدمة' (Introduction), 'منهج الدراسة' (Methodology), and 'الدراسات السابقة' (Previous Studies). This outlines the scholarly process, showing the book is a structured academic study.
The inclusion of 'مسلمة الدراسة' (Premise of the study) indicates an epistemological foundation.

Navigating a Scholarly Work: The Table of Contents in Islamic Epistemology
Lists chapters, sections, and page numbers of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to parse a table of contents from an Islamic epistemology book to identify its structural components and anticipated content.

Core Idea
A table of contents reveals the author's roadmap for building an argument.

This lesson uses the table of contents from 'Nazariyya Quran' to teach you how to extract the logical structure of a scholarly work. By learning to read a table of contents actively, you can anticipate the author's method, locate key discussions, and see how topics relate. This skill is essential for efficiently studying any Islamic discipline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the front matter
Look for introductory sections before the main content: dedication, thanks, preface, introduction. These establish the context and purpose of the work.
In the given table, pages 10-23 contain front matter.
2
Locate the major parts
The main body is divided into parts (e.g., Part One). Each part covers a broad theme. Note the part titles and page ranges.
Part One is 'Introduction to the Theory of Knowledge'.
3
Examine chapter titles
Within each part, chapters (e.g., Chapter One, Chapter Two) break down the theme. Read the chapter titles to infer specific topics covered.
Chapter One covers development of the theory; Chapter Two covers definitions.
4
Look for appendices or back matter
Check if there are indexes, bibliographies, or appendices. These provide additional references and tools.
No appendices are listed here, but other works may have them.
5
Map the logical flow
Consider how the sections build on each other. The author likely starts with foundational concepts before moving to applications or critiques.
The flow here: front matter → part one with development → definitions → further chapters.

Navigating the Book's Structure
Table of contents listing the structure and topics of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two main parts of the book and locate specific topics within them using the table of contents.

Core Idea
A table of contents is a map: it shows the architecture of knowledge before you read.

This is the table of contents for 'Nazariyya Quran'. It lists what the book covers and where. By learning to read this map, you'll be able to place each chapter in context and see how the author organizes Islamic epistemology. Let's walk through its structure.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two major parts
Look at the TOC: there are two main parts (الباب الأول and الباب الثاني). Note their titles: Part One is 'Introduction to the Theory of Knowledge', Part Two is 'The Nature of Knowledge in the Quran and Its Educational Implications'.
2
Scan the chapter titles under each part
Part One has two chapters: one on the development of the theory of knowledge, another on definitions. Part Two has two chapters: one on the ethics and unity of knowledge, another on the domain of knowledge (the unseen and the witnessed).
3
Notice the subtopics listed under each chapter
Under each chapter title there are bullet points listing key themes. For example, under 'Definitions' we see definitions of theory, educational theory, Islamic educational theory, etc. These give you an overview of what each section contains.
4
Relate the structure to Islamic sciences
This TOC shows how the author connects epistemology (Part One) with Quranic concepts and education (Part Two). The categories of 'unseen and witnessed' are classic in Kalam. Understanding this order helps you follow the author's argument.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner

Navigating the Quranic Epistemology: Fields of Knowledge
Lists chapters and sections of the book on Quranic epistemology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to map the two main fields of knowledge (al-ghayb and al-shahada) and their subdivisions as outlined in the Quranic theory of knowledge.

Core Idea
The Quran divides knowledge into the unseen and the witnessed, with the cosmos and the self as its primary domains.

The table of contents of Nazariyya Quran reveals a structured approach to epistemology rooted in the Quran. Understanding this structure is the first step toward grasping how revelation and reason, inner and outer signs, work together. This lesson will guide you through the key divisions and concepts that form the backbone of Quranic epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Survey the overall structure
Notice the main headings: Introduction, Chapter Two, and two sections under Chapter Two. What is the focus of each section?
2
Identify the two fields of knowledge
Section Two explicitly divides knowledge into al-ghayb (the unseen) and al-shahada (the witnessed). Write down the key topics listed under each field.
3
Explore the subdivisions of al-shahada
Under al-shahada, find the subcategories: al-afaq (horizons) and al-anfus (souls). What aspects of each are discussed?
4
Examine the manifestations of al-sunan
Note the list of manifestations under 'laws of the souls': causality, pairing, change, repulsion, trial. How do these relate to the witnessed field?

Source pages p. 11

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents of the book 'Nazariyya Quran' (The Qur'anic Theory). It shows the overall structure of the work. The book is divided into an introduction and a second chapter (likely the main body), which focuses on the nature of knowledge in the Quran and its educational implications. The chapter has two main sections: the first deals with the ethics and unity of knowledge, addressing topics such as the philosophy of knowledge unity, the danger of dualism, and perspectives of believers and People of the Book. The second section discusses the field of knowledge, dividing it into the unseen (al-ghayb) and the witnessed (al-shahada). Under the unseen, it covers its definition, characteristics, reports, knowability, tools, and principles. Under the witnessed, it covers definition, divisions, the relationship between the two fields, and then specific sub-topics: the horizons (آفاق) and the souls (أنفس). Under horizons, it discusses the objectives and characteristics of the 'verses of horizons' (آيات الآفاق). Under souls, it discusses the origin of man, stages of creation, position of man, laws of souls, importance and characteristics of these laws, and their manifestations including causality, pairing, change, repulsion, and trial. The table of contents indicates a systematic approach to Qur'anic epistemology.

C) Ethics of knowledge and philosophy of unity
D) The laws of causality and pairing

Key Takeaway
The Quranic theory of knowledge organizes knowledge into two realms — the unseen and the witnessed — each with its own tools and principles, leading to a comprehensive understanding of reality.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

Navigating the Table of Contents of Nazariyya Quran
Table of contents listing chapters and topics of the book.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to locate specific topics in the table of contents and describe the overall structure of the book Nazariyya Quran.

Core Idea
The table of contents is the roadmap to the author's argument.

This passage is a table of contents (fihris) listing the chapters and topics of the book 'Nazariyya Quran'. Knowing how to read a table of contents is essential for navigating any scholarly work. It reveals the overall plan: definition of testimony, then horizons and souls (آفاق وأنفس), then the sources of knowledge in the Quran. Let us learn to parse it efficiently.

Guided Path
1
Identify the major divisions
Scan the table for repeated headings and page numbers. The first column covers topics like 'التعريف', 'أقسام الشهادة', then 'الآفاق' and 'الأنفس'. The second column introduces 'الباب الثالث' (Chapter Three) on sources of knowledge.
The two-column layout may mix page numbers; focus on the thematic groupings.
2
Extract the chapter structure
Notice that after the initial topics, the TOC lists 'الباب الثالث' with an introduction and two chapters: 'الفصل الأول: الحس' and 'الفصل الثاني: العقل'. This shows the book's progression from core concepts to epistemology.
3
Locate key subtopics
Find specific items like 'السنن' and its manifestations (مظهر السببية, مظهر الزوجية, etc.). These appear under 'الأنفس'. Also locate 'تعريف العقل' and 'أقسام العقل' under the chapter on intellect.
Use the page numbers to jump to the right section.
4
Predict the logical flow
The sequence from 'شهادة' (testimony) to 'آفاق وأنفس' (external and internal signs) to 'مصادر المعرفة' (sources of knowledge) suggests the author builds a case from observable evidence to rational and sensory epistemology.
This helps anticipate the argument before reading.

Commentary
This passage is a table of contents for the book 'Nazariyya Quran'. It lists the main topics and their corresponding page numbers. The first part covers topics such as definition, divisions of testimony, and the relationship between them, followed by a section on 'The Horizons' and 'The Souls', including sub-topics like the origin of man and the manifestations of sunnan (divine laws). The second part introduces Chapter Three, which focuses on the sources and methods of knowledge in the Quran. It begins with an introduction and discussions on terminology and classification, then details two chapters: one on the senses (including external and internal senses) and one on the intellect (its definition, divisions, and role). The student should use this contents page to navigate the book and understand its structure.

Overview: The Four Sources of Knowledge in the Quran
Lists the book's chapters on sources of knowledge

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify and classify the four main sources of knowledge presented in the Quran according to the book's structure.

Core Idea
The Quran's epistemology integrates senses, intellect, revelation, and intuition.

This lesson introduces the comprehensive classification of knowledge sources in the Quran as outlined in 'Nazariyya Quran'. Understanding this structure is foundational for analyzing Islamic epistemology and its educational implications.

Guided Path
1
Memorize the four main sources
Commit to memory the four chapter titles: Senses, Intellect, Revelation, and Secondary Sources (Intuition).
2
Understand the sequence
Note the order: from the most immediate (senses) to the highest (revelation), with secondary sources as supplementary.
3
Identify subcategories
For each source, list the subheadings mentioned (e.g., definition, divisions, etc.) to see the analytical depth.
4
Relate to Islamic sciences
Consider how each source is used in tafsir, fiqh, or kalam: senses for observation of creation, intellect for rational arguments, revelation for divine commands, intuition for inspiration.

الباب الثالث: مصادر المعرفة وطرائقها في القرآن وتضميناتها التربوية. مقدمة. أولاً: تصور بعض الباحثين للمصطلح. ثانياً: خلط بين المصادر والطرائق وبعض عناصر النظرية. تصنيف المصادر والطرائق. الفصل الأول: الحس. تعريف الحس. الفرق بين الحس والتجريب. أنواع الحواس: أولاً: الحواس الظاهرة. ثانياً: الحواس الباطنة. أهمية الحواس. نسبية الحواس. الفصل الثاني: العقل. تعريف العقل. أقسام العقل. فلسفة العقل في القرآن. أهمية العقل: أولاً: مظهر الأساليب العقلية في القرآن. ثانياً: مظهر الحث المتنوع لإعمال العقل. طبيعة عمل العقل. خصائص العقل. صفة السببية. نسبية العقل. موقف القرآن من الحس والعقل (خلاصة). الفصل الثالث: الوحي. تعريف الوحي. ضرورة النبوة. طريق معرفة الوحي. غاية الوحي. خصائص الوحي. طبيعة الوحي. فريق الوحي. أولاً: قواسم الاشتراك. ثانياً: خصوصيات رائد الفريق. التكامل بين الوحي ومصادر المعرفة الأخرى. أولاً: دور العقل في الوحي. ثانياً: دور الوحي في العقل. الفصل الرابع: المصادر التبعية. أولاً: الحدس. تعريف الحدس. أقسام الحدس. أهمية الحدس.

Commentary
This passage is the table of contents for the book 'Nazariyya Quran', specifically for the third chapter which discusses sources and methods of knowledge in the Quran and their educational implications. The author outlines a systematic classification: senses (external and internal), intellect (with its characteristics and causality), revelation (its necessity, purpose, and integration with other sources), and secondary sources, notably intuition. This structure reveals the book's comprehensive approach to epistemology from an Islamic perspective, emphasizing the interplay between sensory experience, rational thought, divine revelation, and intuitive insight. The table of contents serves as a roadmap for the reader, indicating the logical flow from fundamental sources to more derived ones.

Key Takeaway
The four sources of knowledge in the Quran are senses, intellect, revelation, and intuition, each with distinct roles and subcategories.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Using the four-source classification, categorize the following: a verse from the Quran commanding prayer (revelation), the observation that prayer times are determined by the sun (senses), the logical deduction that prayer is obligatory because Allah commanded it (intellect), and a scholar's intuition about the wisdom of prayer (intuition).

Senses as a Source of Knowledge
Lists subheadings for the chapter on senses

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the role of senses in Islamic epistemology and distinguish between external and internal senses.

Core Idea
The senses are the foundation of empirical knowledge in the Quran.

This lesson focuses on the first source of knowledge: senses. The table of contents outlines key aspects: definition, distinction from experimentation, types (external and internal), importance, and relativity. Understanding senses helps us appreciate how the Quran grounds knowledge in tangible experience.

Guided Path
1
Define sensation
Find the definition of 'al-hiss' in classical Islamic thought: sensory perception through five external and five internal senses.
The table of contents does not give the definition, but this is a common classification.
2
Distinguish from experimentation
Note the difference: sensation is direct perception, experimentation is controlled inquiry.
3
List the types
External senses: sight, hearing, smell, taste, touch. Internal senses: common sense, imagination, reflection, memory, estimation.
4
Evaluate the relativity of senses
The Quran acknowledges that senses can be deceived (e.g., mirages) and that ultimate certainty comes only through revelation.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate

Intellect as a Source of Knowledge
Lists subheadings for the chapter on intellect

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to describe the Quranic concept of intellect, its characteristics, and its role in complementing other sources.

Core Idea
The intellect is a divinely given tool for reasoning and understanding revelation.

This lesson examines the second source: intellect. The table of contents covers its definition, divisions, philosophy in the Quran, importance (rational methods and encouragement to use intellect), nature of its work, characteristics, causality, relativity, and a summary of the Quran's stance on intellect and senses. Intellect is presented as an active faculty for processing revelational and empirical data.

Guided Path
1
Define intellect
Define 'al-aql' as the faculty of reasoning, making distinctions, and understanding cause and effect.
The table of contents mentions 'characteristics' and 'attribute of causality'.
2
Outline its divisions
Note the divisions: theoretical intellect (al-aql al-nazari) and practical intellect (al-aql al-amali) - though this may be from the book.
The table of contents lists 'divisions of intellect' without specifying.
3
Identify rational methods in the Quran
The Quran uses rational arguments: analogy, cause and effect, etc. Identify examples like the argument from design.
The table of contents includes 'manifestation of rational methods in the Quran'.
4
Explain causality
The Quran affirms a causal order (sunna of Allah) that the intellect can discern, but also affirms divine omnipotence.
The table of contents specifically mentions 'attribute of causality'.

This passage is the table of contents for the book 'Nazariyya Quran', specifically for the third chapter which discusses sources and methods of knowledge in the Quran and their educational implications. The author outlines a systematic classification: senses (external and internal), intellect (with its characteristics and causality), revelation (its necessity, purpose, and integration with other sources), and secondary sources, notably intuition. The table of contents serves as a roadmap for the reader, indicating the logical flow from fundamental sources to more derived ones.

Introduction and Front Matter
intermediate
7 min
Revelation as the Supreme Source
Lists subheadings for the chapter on revelation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to articulate the necessity and characteristics of revelation as a source of knowledge distinct from senses and intellect.

Core Idea
Revelation provides knowledge inaccessible to senses and intellect alone.

This lesson explores revelation, the third and highest source. The table of contents covers definition, necessity of prophethood, way of knowing revelation, purpose, characteristics, nature, the revelation team, and integration with other sources (roles of intellect and revelation in each other). Revelation is presented as indispensable for guidance beyond human capacity.

Guided Path
1
Define revelation
Define 'al-wahy' as divine communication to prophets, containing guidance and truths about the unseen.
The table of contents includes 'definition of revelation'.
2
Explain prophethood necessity
Senses and intellect cannot provide ultimate knowledge of purpose, afterlife, etc., so revelation is needed.
The table of contents lists 'necessity of prophethood'.
3
Identify revelation's characteristics
Infallible, preserved, comprehensive, and integrated with other sources.
The table of contents includes 'characteristics of revelation'.
4
Describe integration
Revelation and intellect are complementary: revelation provides principles, intellect deduces rulings; intellect must be used to understand revelation.
The table of contents has a section on 'integration between revelation and other sources' with subsections on the role of intellect in revelation and vice versa.

Intuition as a Secondary Source
Lists subheadings for the chapter on secondary sources (intuition)

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define intuition and distinguish it from other sources of knowledge.

Core Idea
Intuition is a spontaneous, inspired knowledge that supplements senses, intellect, and revelation.

This lesson covers the final source: intuition (secondary sources). The table of contents lists definition, divisions, and importance of intuition. Though secondary, intuition plays a role in quick understanding and spiritual insight, but it must be subordinated to revelation and sound intellect.

Guided Path
1
Define intuition
Define 'al-hads' as direct, non-inferential knowledge that arises in the heart or mind, often after purification.
The table of contents includes 'definition of intuition'.
2
Classify types
Divisions may include spiritual inspiration (ilhām) vs. rational intuition (ḥads).
The table of contents includes 'divisions of intuition'.
3
Assess its importance
Intuition can provide swift understanding but is fallible; it must be verified by revelation and sound intellect.
The table of contents includes 'importance of intuition'.
4
Differentiate from revelation
Intuition is not infallible revelation; it is personal and not binding on others.

Navigating the Epistemic Structure of Nazariyya Quran
Table of contents listing chapters and subtopics

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to map the major epistemological sources discussed in Nazariyya Quran: reason, revelation, and subsidiary sources.

Core Idea
The Quranic epistemology integrates reason, revelation, intuition, inspiration, and dreams.

The table of contents of Nazariyya Quran reveals the book's systematic approach to Islamic epistemology. It begins with reason and causality, moves to revelation as the primary source, then to subsidiary sources like intuition, inspiration, and dreams. This lesson will help you navigate the overall structure before diving into each topic.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main divisions
Look at the top-level headings: introductory topics on reason, then Chapter Three on revelation, and Chapter Four on subsidiary sources. Note the logical progression from primary to secondary sources.
The book does not have a separate chapter on reason; it appears as preliminary topics.
2
List the subtopics under each chapter
Under revelation: definition, necessity, way of knowing, purpose, characteristics, nature, team, integration with reason. Under subsidiary sources: intuition, inspiration, true dreams, each with definitions, divisions, and relationship to Quran.
Notice that each subsidiary source has a similar structure: definition, divisions, characteristics, Quranic position.
3
Recognize the hierarchy and relationships
Understand that revelation is primary, subsidiary sources are secondary. Also, each source is examined for its definition, role, and relationship to other sources (e.g., inspiration vs. intuition).
The section on integration between revelation and other sources bridges the chapters.
4
Map the sources to Islamic sciences
Identify which Islamic science each source belongs to: reason in kalam, revelation in usul al-fiqh and tafsir, inspiration in tasawwuf, dreams in hadith and tafsir.
This mapping helps contextualize the book's interdisciplinary approach.
5
Apply the structure to locate specific topics
For example, to find the Quran's view on intuition, look under Chapter Four, section on intuition. To understand the necessity of prophethood, see revelation chapter.
This skill is useful for quick reference when studying the book.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
10 min
Overview of Quranic Epistemology: Intuition, Inspiration, Dreams, Doubt, and Certainty
Lists the book's chapters and topics covering intuition, inspiration, true dreams, doubt, and certainty.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to map the major epistemological concepts covered in Nazariyya al-Quran and identify how they relate to doubt and certainty.

Core Idea
The Quran's epistemology addresses intuition, inspiration, dreams, doubt, and certainty as interconnected pathways to knowledge.

This lesson introduces the structural roadmap of the book 'Nazariyya al-Quran' (The Quranic Theory of Knowledge). The table of contents reveals the author's plan: after exploring non-sensory sources like intuition and inspiration, the work tackles true dreams, then moves to the central pair of doubt and certainty. Understanding this map will help you see the logical flow from foundational concepts to the possibility of knowledge itself. Let's unpack the blueprint.

Guided Path
1
Locate the three main post-introductory topics
The ToC lists intuition, inspiration, and true dreams as consecutive sections. Notice how each builds on the previous: from individual intuition to communicated inspiration to shared dreams.
These three are grouped under 'محتوى' (Content) on page 15.
2
Identify the shift to doubt and certainty
After the dream section, the book transitions to 'Knowledge between doubt and certainty.' This signals the epistemological core: the tension between skepticism and conviction.
This is the beginning of 'الباب الرابع' (Chapter Four) on page 16.
3
Note the subdivisions within doubt and certainty
Doubt is split into absolute and methodological; certainty has levels and a model from al-Ghazali. This shows the author's analytical treatment of epistemic states.
Pay attention to 'الشك المطلق' vs 'الشك المنهجي' and 'مراتب اليقين'.
4
Recognize the final chapter on cognitive truth
Chapter Two discusses the possibility of obtaining truth, including the difference between haqq and haqiqa. This concludes the epistemological inquiry.
The last subtopic 'الفرق بين الحق والحقيقة' is a key distinction.

Commentary
This passage is a table of contents for the book 'Nazariyya Quran', outlining its structure. It begins by listing topics covered on page 15: characteristics of intuition (al-hads), the Quran's stance on it, then inspiration (al-ilham) with its definition, divisions, difference from intuition, relationship to reason and senses, and scientific thinking. Next are true dreams (al-ru'ya al-sadiqa), their definition, levels (prophets vs. believers), and types (righteous, anxieties of wakefulness, terrifying), and the Islamic stance. Page 16 presents Chapter Four on the possibility of obtaining knowledge in the Quran and its educational implications. It contains two chapters: Chapter One on knowledge between doubt and certainty, covering doubt (roots, absolute and methodological), the Quran's stance, intrinsic and acquired possibility, then certainty (legitimacy, prophetic methodology, Quranic stance, levels of certainty, and al-Ghazali's methodological doubt). Chapter Two discusses the possibility of obtaining cognitive truth, including the difference between right (haqq) and truth (haqiqa). This front matter serves as a roadmap for readers.

Introduction and Front Matter

Reading the Logical Map of Nazariyya Quran
Table of contents listing the book's main topics of discussion.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to infer the author's research methodology and philosophical approach from the table of contents of Nazariyya Quran.

Core Idea
A table of contents is a logical map of the author's argument.

When you open a scholarly work, the table of contents is not just a list of topics. It reveals the author's method: where they start, how they build concepts, and what they aim to conclude. This lesson will help you decode the structure of Nazariyya Quran from its table of contents, so you can anticipate the logical flow before reading the full text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the main sections
Look at the Arabic headings. Notice the major divisions: linguistic difference, terminological difference, divisions of truth, limits of truth, philosophy of truth in the Quran, the Quran as the book of truth, rules of research, conclusion, and appendices.
The list moves from simple to complex and from linguistic to philosophical.
2
Observe the progression of content
The author starts with a linguistic distinction (الفرق اللغوي), then moves to terminological (الفرق الاصطلاحي). This shows a move from everyday language to technical definition. Then 'divisions of truth' (أقسام الحقيقة) and 'limits of truth' (حدود الحقيقة) suggest a systematic classification and boundary-setting.
This sequence reflects a classical method: first clarify terms, then categorize, then investigate.
3
Connect to the Quranic focus
After the foundational chapters, the book turns to 'Philosophy of truth in the Quran' and 'The Quran is the book of truth'. This indicates that the earlier conceptual work is applied to the Quran. Finally, 'Rules of research for truth' provides a methodological toolkit.
The author is grounding a Quranic theory of truth on careful conceptual analysis.
4
Infer the author's purpose
The appendix lists key Quranic verses on epistemology, and the bibliography includes diverse sources. This suggests the author aims to produce a comprehensive, evidence-based study integrating linguistic, philosophical, and Quranic perspectives.
A table of contents can often reveal whether a work is purely theoretical or also practical.

Commentary
This passage presents the table of contents of the book, outlining its structure. The first topic is the linguistic distinction regarding truth, followed by the terminological distinction. Then the author divides truth into its categories, then discusses its boundaries. Next is the philosophy of truth in the Quran, affirming the Quran as the book of truth. Then rules for seeking truth are presented. The book concludes with an appendix listing key Quranic verses related to epistemology, and a bibliography divided into books, periodicals, conference proceedings, and foreign sources. This table of contents shows the comprehensive approach of the book to the subject of truth from both linguistic and philosophical perspectives within a Quranic framework.

Quranic Foundations of Knowledge
Author cites Quranic verses glorifying knowledge and scholars.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the Quranic verses cited to establish the virtue of knowledge and explain how each verse supports the author's thesis.

Core Idea
Knowledge is a divine gift and the path to fearing Allah, setting the stage for logical inquiry.

Before diving into the technical discussions of Mantiq, the author grounds the entire work in a Quranic worldview. This lesson examines five key verses that the author uses to elevate the status of knowledge and the knowledgeable. Understanding this foundation will help you see why logical reasoning is an act of worship, not merely an intellectual exercise.

Guided Path
1
List the Verses
Identify the five Quranic verses cited by the author: Surah al-Mujadilah (58:11), Surah al-Isra (17:85), Surah Yusuf (12:76), Surah Taha (20:114), and Surah Fatir (35:27-28).
The verses are presented in a specific order to build the author's argument incrementally.
2
Analyze Each Verse's Contribution
For each verse, determine what it says about knowledge or the knowledgeable. Verse 58:11 promises elevation; 17:85 limits human knowledge; 12:76 places Allah above all knowers; 20:114 commands seeking increase in knowledge; 35:27-28 connects knowledge to the fear of Allah.
Pay attention to the logical progression: from reward, to limitation, to divine supremacy, to command, to the purpose of knowledge.
3
Synthesize the Overall Message
Combine the insights: Knowledge is a divine gift that elevates, is limited in humans, and ultimately leads to fearing Allah. This forms the theological premise for the study of logic.
The author uses these verses to show that Mantiq, as a tool for knowledge, aligns with Quranic values.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بسم الله الرحمن الرحيم
ويرفع الله الذين آمنوا منكم والذين أوتوا العلم درجات والله بما تعملون خبير [المجادلة: 11]
وما أوتيتم من العلم إلا قليلاً [الإسراء: 85]
نرفع درجات من نشاء وفوق كل ذي علم عليم [يوسف: 76]
وقل رب زدني علما [طه: 114]
ألم تر أن الله أنزل من السماء ماء فأخرجنا به ثمرات مختلفاً ألوانها، ومن الجبال جدد بيض وحمر مختلف ألوانها وغرابيب سود * ومن الناس والدواب والأنعام مختلف ألوانه كذلك، إنما يخشى الله من عباده العلماء إن الله عزيز غفور [فاطر: 27-28]
In the name of Allah, the Most Gracious, the Most Merciful. Allah will raise those who have believed among you and those who were given knowledge, by degrees. And Allah is Acquainted with what you do. [Quran 58:11] And you have not been given of knowledge except a little. [Quran 17:85] We raise in degrees whom We will, and over every possessor of knowledge is one [more] knowing. [Quran 12:76] And say, 'My Lord, increase me in knowledge.' [Quran 20:114] Do you not see that Allah sends down rain from the sky, and We produce thereby fruits of varying colors? And in the mountains are tracts, white and red of varying colors and [others] intensely black. And among people and moving creatures and grazing livestock are various colors similarly. Only those fear Allah, from among His servants, who have knowledge. Indeed, Allah is Exalted in Might and Forgiving. [Quran 35:27-28]
Source pages p. 18

Commentary
This passage is an introductory collection of Quranic verses that the author presents to establish the importance and virtue of knowledge ('ilm) before delving into the subject of logic. The passage begins with the basmalah and then cites five verses: The first (58:11) promises elevation in degrees for believers and those given knowledge. The second (17:85) reminds that human knowledge is limited. The third (12:76) states that Allah raises whom He wills and that above every knowledgeable person is One more knowing (Allah). The fourth (20:114) is a command for the Prophet to seek increase in knowledge. The fifth (35:27-28) reflects on the diversity of creation—fruits, mountains, humans, animals—and concludes that only the knowledgeable truly fear Allah. These verses collectively establish the Quranic worldview that knowledge is a divine gift and a path to fearing Allah, setting the stage for the logical discussions to follow.

Dedication to Pioneers of Islamic Education Revival
Author dedicates the work to proponents of Islamic educational theory.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the author's target audience and their defining characteristics based on the dedication's language.

Core Idea
Reviving Islamic education requires pioneers armed with both sacred and secular knowledge.

This dedication reveals the author's vision: a call to a specific group of scholars and educators who are working to develop a contemporary Islamic educational theory that is authentic and renewed, resisting Western cultural dominance. The passage sets the stage for the entire work by defining its target audience and purpose.

Guided Path
1
Identify the target audience
Find the specific group the author addresses. Look for phrases like 'رواد إحياء دور التربية الإسلامية'.
2
List the qualifications of this group
What qualities does the author emphasize? Note the three types of knowledge mentioned: vast specialized knowledge, good culture in Islamic sciences, and distinguished research and methodological skills.
3
Analyze the challenge
What is the author's critique of the current state? Find the concepts of 'الاستلاب والتغريب' and the contrast with 'التحديث والتجديد'.
4
Assess the author's tone
Is the tone optimistic, accusatory, or hopeful? How does the author position these pioneers in relation to the broader narrative of Islamic revival?

الإهداء

إلى رواد إحياء دور التربية الإسلامية الساعين نحو بلورة نظريتها التربوية المعاصرة، الداعين إلى إحلال فلسفتها الأصيلة المتجدّدة محل نظريات الاستلاب والتغريب الثقافي والحضاري بدعاوى التحديث والتجديد !!

إلى هؤلاء المتسلحين بعلم غزير في التخصص، وثقافة جيدة في علوم الشريعة، ومهارات بحثية ومنهجية متميزة في دراسة العلوم الإنسانية والاجتماعية، كي لا يجمدوا ... أو يُستَلَبوا ... أو يسطّحوا..
محسدين بذلك توازن الشخصية المسلمة، ووسطية الدين الحنيف واعتدال الوجهة التربوية القويمة.
وليس ذلك غريباً فهؤلاء الروّاد أنفسهم إحدى الثمار الطيبة لهذه التربية المنشودة، وإن جاءت في زمن الاغتراب وهيمنة أقوياء الحضارة الغربية.
وهم كذلك مُخرج حي من مخرجاتها في التغيير الفاعل البعيد.
وعلى أيديهم - بإذن الله - ينبلج الصبح وتشرق شمس الغد الواعد بجيل
النصر المنشود، وما ذلك على الله بعزيز.

إلى هؤلاء الأمل ... أهدي هذا العمل

...
والله من وراء القصد..
The Dedication

To the pioneers of reviving the role of Islamic education, striving to crystallize its contemporary educational theory, calling for replacing its authentic renewed philosophy with theories of cultural and civilizational alienation and Westernization under the guise of modernization and renewal!!

To those armed with vast specialized knowledge, good culture in the Islamic sciences, and distinguished research and methodological skills in studying the humanities and social sciences, so that they do not stagnate... or be alienated... or be flattened..
Envious of that balance of the Muslim personality, the moderation of the upright religion, and the moderation of the sound educational orientation.
And that is not strange, for these pioneers themselves are one of the good fruits of this desired education, even if they come in a time of alienation and dominance of the powerful from Western civilization.
And they are likewise a living product of its outputs in effective distant change.
And at their hands - by Allah's permission - the dawn breaks and the sun of a promising tomorrow rises with a generation of the awaited victory, and that is not difficult for Allah.

To these hopeful ones... I dedicate this work

...
And Allah is behind the intention..
Source pages p. 21

Commentary
This passage is a dedication (الإهداء) from the book 'Nazariyya Quran'. The author begins by addressing a specific audience: the pioneers who are working to revive Islamic education. These individuals are described as seeking to develop a contemporary educational theory based on authentic Islamic philosophy, replacing Western theories of cultural and civilizational alienation. The author emphasizes that these pioneers are well-equipped with specialized knowledge, a good foundation in Islamic sciences, and strong research skills in the humanities and social sciences. The dedication praises their balanced Muslim personality and moderate educational approach, noting that they are themselves products of the very education they strive for. The author expresses hope that through their efforts, a victorious generation will emerge, and concludes by dedicating the work to them.

The Quran as a Comprehensive Creed
Author introduces the Quran's comprehensive role in addressing epistemological problems.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain how the Quran functions as a comprehensive creed (ʿaqīda kulliyya) that shapes the Muslim worldview.

Core Idea
The Quran's creed encompasses man, universe, and life.

This passage asserts that the Quran is not just a book of rituals but a comprehensive creed that determines a Muslim's entire worldview. Understanding this foundational claim helps us see how the Quran addresses all aspects of existence, not just the spiritual. Let's break down what this means and how the author supports it.

Guided Path
1
Extract the three domains
Find in the passage the three domains the Quranic creed addresses: man, the universe, and life. These are explicitly mentioned.
2
Analyze the term 'determines'
Consider what it means for the creed to 'determine' (tuḥaddid) the conception. It implies shaping and guiding thought, not just informing.
3
Connect to methodology
Note how the author links this creed to the methodology of inclusion and transcendence: it encompasses past and extends to future.
4
Apply to education
Reflect on the author's remark that societal problems stem from weak education. How does this creed relate to educational reform?

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مُقدمة
يمثل القرآن الكريم - بالنسبة إلى المسلم - عقيدة كلية، تعمل على تحديد تصوره للإنسان والكون والحياة، نظراً لما يزخر به من قضايا وأفكار وموضوعات ذات أبعاد خالدة، استوعبت الماضي، وتجاوزت إلى الحاضر، وامتدت بآفاقها نحو المستقبل، وفق منهج متميز يمكن وصفه بمنهج الاستيعاب والتجاوز. ويظهر للباحث في ميدان التربية الإسلامية مدى صلة القرآن الكريم بوصفه معينًا دافقاً - بمعالجة مشكلات المجتمع ، ثقافية كانت أم أخلاقية، بحسبانها جميعًا تداعيات تلقائية لتربية خربة، أو ضعيفة في أحسن الأحوال.
ولعلّ قضية المعرفة إحدى أهم المشكلات المعاصرة، من حيث رؤيتها الفلسفية، لطبيعة هذه المعرفة ومصادرها وطرائقها وإمكان الحصول عليها، بما يمكن أن تُشكل مجتمعة ما يعرف بـ (نظرية المعرفة). وقد حفل القرآن الكريم بتناول هذه العناصر التي تعتمد عليها النظرية، بما يؤكد شموليته واستيعابه و خلوده (۱) . وبالنسبة إلى مجال التربية فإن الأمر أعقد نتيجة التعدد المتناقض لنظريات التربية في العالم. وعلى الرغم من أن مدارس كالمثالية والواقعية والوجودية والبراجماتية ذات منشأ غربي ولذلك فهي تصنف في إطار التربية الغربية، إلا أن حجم التباين التضادي بينها، وما تولّد عن كل واحدة منهـا مـن تفريعات؛ يفوق مساحة هذه السطور سرداً وتوصيفاً وتقويماً.
(۱) راجع في ذلك الدراسات التي تمت بهذا الخصوص كوجهة عامة، وأبرزها: نظرية المعرفة بين القرآن والفلسفة لراجح الكردي، ومقالة في المعرفة لعدنان زرزور وقضايا المعرفة لسعيد إسماعيل علي.
Introduction
The Holy Quran — for the Muslim — represents a comprehensive creed that works to determine his conception of man, the universe, and life, given what it abounds in of issues, ideas, and topics of eternal dimensions, which encompassed the past, transcended to the present, and extended with its horizons towards the future, according to a distinguished methodology that can be described as the methodology of inclusion and transcendence. It appears to the researcher in the field of Islamic education the extent of the relevance of the Holy Quran as a flowing source — in addressing society's problems, whether cultural or moral, considering them all as spontaneous repercussions of a ruined education, or at best a weak one.
Perhaps the issue of knowledge is one of the most important contemporary problems, in terms of its philosophical vision, regarding the nature of this knowledge, its sources, its methods, and the possibility of obtaining it, which together can form what is known as (theory of knowledge). The Holy Quran has been replete with addressing these elements upon which the theory depends, confirming its comprehensiveness, inclusiveness, and eternity (1). As for the field of education, the matter is more complex due to the contradictory multiplicity of educational theories in the world. Despite the fact that schools such as Idealism, Realism, Existentialism, and Pragmatism are of Western origin and therefore are classified within the framework of Western education, the extent of antagonistic disparity between them, and what each one produced of ramifications, exceeds the space of these lines for narration, description, and evaluation.
(1) Refer in that regard to the studies conducted on this topic in general, most notably: Theory of Knowledge between the Quran and Philosophy by Rajih al-Kurdi, and an Article on Knowledge by Adnan Zarzur, and Issues of Knowledge by Sa'id Ismail Ali.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is an introduction from the book 'Nazariyya Quran', setting the stage for discussing the Quran's theory of knowledge. The author begins by asserting that the Quran presents a comprehensive creed that shapes the Muslim's worldview regarding man, the universe, and life. This creed is described as having a distinctive methodology of 'inclusion and transcendence' (istīʿāb wa tajāwuz), meaning it encompasses past knowledge, addresses present concerns, and extends to future horizons. The author then highlights the relevance of the Quran as a flowing source for solving societal problems—cultural and moral—which are seen as consequences of flawed or weak education.

The focus then shifts to epistemology (qaḍiyyat al-maʿrifa), identified as a key contemporary problem. The author notes that epistemology philosophically examines the nature, sources, methods, and attainability of knowledge. The Quran, it is claimed, addresses all these elements, confirming its comprehensiveness and timelessness. A footnote references key studies on this topic. Finally, the author contrasts the Quranic approach with Western educational theories (Idealism, Realism, Existentialism, Pragmatism), which are diverse and contradictory, and notes that their detailed exposition is beyond the scope of this introduction. The passage thus establishes the Quran's epistemological framework as superior and holistic, while acknowledging the complexity of contemporary educational discourse.

Key Terms
عقيدة كلية
منهج الاستيعاب والتجاوز

Key Takeaway

The Quran's Epistemological Role
Author introduces the Quran's comprehensive role in addressing epistemological problems.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the epistemological elements (nature, sources, methods, attainability) that the Quran addresses according to the author.

Core Idea
The Quran comprehensively covers all elements of epistemology.

The author identifies epistemology (naẓariyyat al-maʿrifa) as a key contemporary problem. He claims that the Quran addresses all its core elements: the nature of knowledge, its sources, its methods, and its attainability. This lesson unpacks that claim and contrasts it with Western educational theories.

Guided Path
1
Define epistemology from the passage
Locate the sentence where the author defines 'theory of knowledge' (naẓariyyat al-maʿrifa). It lists four elements: nature, sources, methods, and possibility of obtaining knowledge.
2
Extract the Quran's claim
Find the author's statement that the Quran has addressed these elements, confirming its comprehensive nature.
3
Contrast with Western theories
The author mentions that Western theories (Idealism, Realism, Existentialism, Pragmatism) are contradictory. Note how this contrast highlights the Quran's unified approach.
4
Evaluate the claim
Given the footnote referencing studies, think about how one might verify this claim by looking at Quranic verses on knowledge.

مُقدمة
يمثل القرآن الكريم - بالنسبة إلى المسلم - عقيدة كلية، تعمل على تحديد تصوره للإنسان والكون والحياة، نظراً لما يزخر به من قضايا وأفكار وموضوعات ذات أبعاد خالدة، استوعبت الماضي، وتجاوزت إلى الحاضر، وامتدت بآفاقها نحو المستقبل، وفق منهج متميز يمكن وصفه بمنهج الاستيعاب والتجاوز. ويظهر للباحث في ميدان التربية الإسلامية مدى صلة القرآن الكريم بوصفه معينًا دافقاً - بمعالجة مشكلات المجتمع ، ثقافية كانت أم أخلاقية، بحسبانها جميعًا تداعيات تلقائية لتربية خربة، أو ضعيفة في أحسن الأحوال.
ولعلّ قضية المعرفة إحدى أهم المشكلات المعاصرة، من حيث رؤيتها الفلسفية، لطبيعة هذه المعرفة ومصادرها وطرائقها وإمكان الحصول عليها، بما يمكن أن تُشكل مجتمعة ما يعرف بـ (نظرية المعرفة). وقد حفل القرآن الكريم بتناول هذه العناصر التي تعتمد عليها النظرية، بما يؤكد شموليته واستيعابه و خلوده (۱) . وبالنسبة إلى مجال التربية فإن الأمر أعقد نتيجة التعدد المتناقض لنظريات التربية في العالم. وعلى الرغم من أن مدارس كالمثالية والواقعية والوجودية والبراجماتية ذات منشأ غربي ولذلك فهي تصنف في إطار التربية الغربية، إلا أن حجم التباين التضادي بينها، وما تولّد عن كل واحدة منهـا مـن تفريعات؛ يفوق مساحة هذه السطور سرداً وتوصيفاً وتقويماً.
(۱) راجع في ذلك الدراسات التي تمت بهذا الخصوص كوجهة عامة، وأبرزها: نظرية المعرفة بين القرآن والفلسفة لراجح الكردي، ومقالة في المعرفة لعدنان زرزور وقضايا المعرفة لسعيد إسماعيل علي.
Introduction
The Holy Quran — for the Muslim — represents a comprehensive creed that works to determine his conception of man, the universe, and life, given what it abounds in of issues, ideas, and topics of eternal dimensions, which encompassed the past, transcended to the present, and extended with its horizons towards the future, according to a distinguished methodology that can be described as the methodology of inclusion and transcendence. It appears to the researcher in the field of Islamic education the extent of the relevance of the Holy Quran as a flowing source — in addressing society's problems, whether cultural or moral, considering them all as spontaneous repercussions of a ruined education, or at best a weak one.
Perhaps the issue of knowledge is one of the most important contemporary problems, in terms of its philosophical vision, regarding the nature of this knowledge, its sources, its methods, and the possibility of obtaining it, which together can form what is known as (theory of knowledge). The Holy Quran has been replete with addressing these elements upon which the theory depends, confirming its comprehensiveness, inclusiveness, and eternity (1). As for the field of education, the matter is more complex due to the contradictory multiplicity of educational theories in the world. Despite the fact that schools such as Idealism, Realism, Existentialism, and Pragmatism are of Western origin and therefore are classified within the framework of Western education, the extent of antagonistic disparity between them, and what each one produced of ramifications, exceeds the space of these lines for narration, description, and evaluation.
(1) Refer in that regard to the studies conducted on this topic in general, most notably: Theory of Knowledge between the Quran and Philosophy by Rajih al-Kurdi, and an Article on Knowledge by Adnan Zarzur, and Issues of Knowledge by Sa'id Ismail Ali.
Source pages p. 26

Commentary
This passage is an introduction from the book 'Nazariyya Quran', setting the stage for discussing the Quran's theory of knowledge. The author begins by asserting that the Quran presents a comprehensive creed that shapes the Muslim's worldview regarding man, the universe, and life. The author then highlights the relevance of the Quran as a flowing source for solving societal problems—cultural and moral—which are seen as consequences of flawed or weak education.

The focus then shifts to epistemology (qaḍiyyat al-maʿrifa), identified as a key contemporary problem. The author notes that epistemology philosophically examines the nature, sources, methods, and attainability of knowledge. The Quran, it is claimed, addresses all these elements, confirming its comprehensiveness and timelessness. A footnote references key studies on this topic. Finally, the author contrasts the Quranic approach with Western educational theories (Idealism, Realism, Existentialism, Pragmatism), which are diverse and contradictory, and notes that their detailed exposition is beyond the scope of this introduction. The passage thus establishes the Quran's epistemological framework as superior and holistic, while acknowledging the complexity of contemporary educational discourse.

Introduction and Front Matter
beginner
5 min
The Need for a Qur'anic Epistemology in Education
Author introduces the need for an Islamic theory of knowledge derived from the Qur'an.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the main premise of the study and explain why the author argues for an Islamic theory of knowledge derived from the Qur'an.

Core Idea
The Qur'an offers a comprehensive, integrated, and eternal framework for knowledge.

This passage introduces the foundational argument of the study: the Qur'an provides a complete worldview and methodology that must guide Islamic education. The author contrasts the comprehensiveness of Qur'anic knowledge with the fragmentation of Western theories, setting the stage for deriving an Islamic educational epistemology.

Guided Path
1
Identify the author's description of the Qur'an
Notice how the author describes the Qur'an as a comprehensive creed ('aqidah kulliyah) that shapes man's conception of existence, encompassing the past, present, and future with a 'methodology of comprehension and transcendence'.
This sets the foundation for why the Qur'an is the source of an Islamic theory of knowledge.
2
Understand the problem in contemporary education
Find where the author criticizes Western educational theories (idealism, realism, etc.) as contradictory and harmful to Muslim youth, and links educational problems to a 'corrupt' or weak education.
This motivates the need for an alternative rooted in the Qur'an.
3
Recognize the relationship between education and epistemology
The author states that the relationship between educational theory and theory of knowledge is that of general to specific (or whole to part). This means a sound education requires a sound epistemological foundation.
4
State the main premise of the study
Locate the explicit premise: 'Qur'anic knowledge is characterized by comprehensiveness, integration, eternity, and absoluteness.' This premise drives the entire research.
This is the key claim you need to remember.

For the Muslim, the Noble Qur'an represents a comprehensive creed that works to determine his conception of man, the universe, and life, due to its abundance of issues, ideas, and subjects of eternal dimensions, which encompassed the past, transcended to the present, and extended with its horizons toward the future, according to a distinguished methodology that can be described as the methodology of comprehension and transcendence. It appears to the researcher in the field of Islamic education the extent of the relevance of the Noble Qur'an as a gushing spring - in addressing society's problems, whether cultural or moral, considering them all as spontaneous repercussions of a corrupt education, or weak at best. Perhaps the issue of knowledge is one of the most important contemporary problems, in terms of its philosophical vision, concerning the nature of this knowledge, its sources, its methods, and the possibility of obtaining it, which together can form what is known as (theory of knowledge). The Noble Qur'an has abounded in addressing these elements upon which the theory depends, confirming its comprehensiveness, inclusiveness, and eternity (1). As for the field of education, the matter is more complicated as a result of the contradictory multiplicity of educational theories in the world. Although schools such as idealism, realism, existentialism, and pragmatism have a Western origin and therefore are classified within the framework of Western education, the extent of the contradictory disparity between them, and what each one generated of subdivisions, exceeds the space of these lines in narration, description, and evaluation. (1) See in that regard the studies that have been done on this subject as a general perspective, most notably: Theory of Knowledge between the Qur'an and Philosophy by Rajih al-Kurdi, and an article on knowledge by Adnan Zarzur, and Issues of Knowledge by Sa'id Ismail Ali. However, the matter that concerns the Muslim researcher today is - primarily - the vision of the Islamic educational philosophy regarding the issue of knowledge from the previous angles, and how it can be reflected on the contemporary Islamic educational reality to meet the need of the contemporary Muslim and the contemporary Islamic society, in replacing the elements of the desired Islamic educational theory with the Western educational theories that scatter the minds of the youth and hinder their launching from their civilizational self and their doctrinal identity. The conflict of ideologies in the field of education in particular necessitates that the Muslim researcher strive to present his Islamic educational theory in various aspects, including the aspect of knowledge, due to its importance stemming from being the embodiment of his civilizational stance in the foundations of education and its subsequent effects on the educational reality. That is because the relationship between educational theory and theory of knowledge is a relationship of the general to the specific, or the whole to the part, as will be indicated in its appropriate place in this study. The Premise of the Study: This study proceeds from a main premise whose content is that Qur'anic knowledge is characterized by comprehensiveness, integration, eternity, and absoluteness, in a manner that urges the researcher to work on eliciting the texts of divine revelation, the Noble Qur'an, to extract an epistemological theory in Islamic education that meets the need of this education and contributes to crystallizing its contemporary theory. The Reason for Selection: The main reason for selecting this study lies in the absence of academic studies - with sound foundations - that have singled out the Qur'an for research in (educational epistemology) despite the availability of studies that research the theory of knowledge in the Noble Qur'an or any

Commentary
This passage is the introduction to a study on educational epistemology in the Qur'an. The author begins by establishing the Qur'an's comprehensive nature as a creed that shapes the Muslim's worldview across time, using a 'methodology of comprehension and transcendence.' He then highlights the crisis of knowledge in contemporary education, noting the conflicting Western educational theories. The author argues that Islamic education must derive its theory of knowledge from the Qur'an, which already addresses the elements of epistemology. He sets up the main premise: Qur'anic knowledge is comprehensive, integrated, eternal, and absolute. The study aims to extract an Islamic educational theory from the Qur'an, filling a gap in academic research.
